## Section 001: Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not define the version-pinned run lifecycle, graph questions, evidence limits, or handoff to direct code reading
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because correct run identity and coverage are prerequisites for trustworthy topology, while question-specific forward and reverse traces reduce context without pretending the graph is runtime execution
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: exact branch behavior, value propagation, reflection, generated code, queues, or dynamic dispatch governs the answer; the graph is stale; or version and bound URL cannot be verified
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for Parseltongue 1.7.2 graph workflows, not generic GitHub automation or exact dynamic analysis
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a versioned run contract, question classifier, orientation and coverage gates, graph-evidence limits, direct-read handoff, and auditable query packet
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Parseltongue is a hypothesis accelerator: its strongest contribution is reducing the search space and exposing topology, not replacing semantic code or runtime evidence
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to pin and verify version 1.7.2, create or refresh an isolated run, load actual paths and server URL from `run.config`, verify health and coverage, orient before tracing, choose the smallest endpoint workflow matching the question, preserve query artifacts, and confirm dynamic or low-coverage conclusions in source
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because correct run identity and coverage are prerequisites for trustworthy topology, while question-specific forward and reverse traces reduce context without pretending the graph is runtime execution
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; exact branch behavior, value propagation, reflection, generated code, queues, or dynamic dispatch governs the answer; the graph is stale; or version and bound URL cannot be verified
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this reference for Parseltongue 1.7.2 graph workflows, not generic GitHub automation or exact dynamic analysis
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add a versioned run contract, question classifier, orientation and coverage gates, graph-evidence limits, direct-read handoff, and auditable query packet
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Parseltongue Graph Workflow Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies Parseltongue is a hypothesis accelerator: its strongest contribution is reducing the search space and exposing topology, not replacing semantic code or runtime evidence

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists four directly relevant local Parseltongue artifacts beside three public workflow links, but its uniform row shape can imply that every source has equal authority over graph behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because provenance determines what a claim can legitimately say; a local endpoint catalog can establish a route contract while a generic CI page can only suggest review or automation practices
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a public automation page is cited as proof of graph traversal, a local heuristic is promoted to runtime fact, a URL is assumed fresh without review, or an inference has no visible evidence chain
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply this hierarchy to the seven frozen source rows and to claims derived from them; do not infer source quality from local-versus-public location alone
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add claim classes, authority rules, misuse examples, conflict handling, and a verification ledger while retaining every original path, URL, category, and synthesis role
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that source authority is claim-relative: the same row may be canonical for installation policy, supporting for a workflow, and irrelevant to a dynamic-control-flow conclusion

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed supplies one repository-generation verifier command, which checks an artifact stage but cannot establish live Parseltongue version, run identity, index health, endpoint responses, or semantic correctness
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because artifact correctness and investigation correctness are orthogonal: a perfectly validated guide can be misapplied to a stale run, while a healthy run cannot excuse a malformed evidence packet
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the archive verifier is treated as proof of graph accuracy, health alone is treated as proof of coverage, a query returning HTTP success is treated as proof of interpretation, or validation output is not preserved
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: distinguish repository-reference QA from target-codebase graph QA and never let evidence from one layer certify the other
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a layered gate matrix, exact evidence packet, pass and fail interpretation, recovery per layer, and the focused validator while retaining the original archive-stage command

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed routes tasks by theme mention and recommends local-first evidence, but it does not help an agent choose among orientation, backward tracing, forward tracing, architecture analysis, context budgeting, or direct reading
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because question classification aligns endpoint direction with the decision and prevents broad graph exploration from consuming time without reducing uncertainty
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the user needs exact values or temporal behavior, no stable entity can be found, parser coverage excludes the surface, the repository is already small and known, or graph setup costs exceed likely narrowing benefit
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: activate for structural codebase questions where Parseltongue 1.7.2 is available or can be safely prepared; do not activate solely because the task says graph or workflow
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace keyword routing with a decision tree covering prerequisites, endpoint direction, stopping rules, direct-evidence exits, and a compact activation audit
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the fastest graph workflow is often the one that knows when to terminate; stopping after a decisive narrowing result protects both context and epistemic clarity

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each step removes a different uncertainty in order: environment identity, repository shape, entity identity, dependency topology, and finally program semantics
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the user expects a one-command diagnosis, the symptom is operational rather than structural, setup cannot be isolated, the entity surface is unparsed, or the trace grows without converging on a reviewable corridor
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this scenario for onboarding, code archaeology, refactor scoping, and structural bug hypotheses, while routing live production diagnosis to telemetry-first workflows

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed offers adopt, adapt, avoid, and cost-of-being-wrong rows around source agreement, but it does not compare Parseltongue setup cost, graph reach, semantic limits, index freshness, or repeat-use value
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the relevant tradeoff is not graph versus no graph in the abstract; it is narrowing benefit and repeatability versus setup, staleness, parser gaps, and semantic confirmation cost
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: adopt is triggered merely by local/external agreement, adapt hides an invalid substrate, avoid means abandoning all evidence gathering, or cost of being wrong is expressed only as wasted time
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply tradeoffs per question and per claim rather than approving or rejecting the tool for an entire repository once
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to reframe adopt, adapt, avoid, and wrong-cost rows around run validity, structural fit, semantic depth, repeat value, and reversible partial use
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that partial use is a first-class outcome: Parseltongue can validly narrow ownership or topology even when it cannot support the final behavioral claim
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to adopt when the run is healthy and the question is structural, adapt when coverage or workflow shape is partial, avoid when exact dynamic behavior dominates, and explicitly account for wrong-run and overreach costs
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the relevant tradeoff is not graph versus no graph in the abstract; it is narrowing benefit and repeatability versus setup, staleness, parser gaps, and semantic confirmation cost

- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: reframe adopt, adapt, avoid, and wrong-cost rows around run validity, structural fit, semantic depth, repeat value, and reversible partial use

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed labels the skill canonical and all three reference files supporting, but it does not specify conflict resolution among archived prose, live API help, run configuration, server output, and repository source
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because authority changes with the question: static policy cannot reveal an auto-incremented port, a workflow cannot override a live route contract, and a graph service cannot determine unmodeled target behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: canonical is interpreted as universally superior, live output silently rewrites archived policy, a supporting heuristic overrides endpoint behavior, or target code is ignored because the graph response appears complete
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use canonical and supporting labels for archived corpus organization, then incorporate live and target-code evidence by claim class without rewriting frozen source roles
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a claim-relative precedence matrix, conflict ledger, examples of legitimate overrides, same-level tie handling, and refresh obligations
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a hierarchy is a routing function, not a prestige ladder; its purpose is to send each question to the evidence capable of answering it
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to use the skill for pinned-version policy, `run.config` and logs for this run's facts, live API documentation for exposed routes, detail references for workflow design, and target source or runtime evidence for program semantics
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because authority changes with the question: static policy cannot reveal an auto-incremented port, a workflow cannot override a live route contract, and a graph service cannot determine unmodeled target behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; canonical is interpreted as universally superior, live output silently rewrites archived policy, a supporting heuristic overrides endpoint behavior, or target code is ignored because the graph response appears complete
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use canonical and supporting labels for archived corpus organization, then incorporate live and target-code evidence by claim class without rewriting frozen source roles
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add a claim-relative precedence matrix, conflict ledger, examples of legitimate overrides, same-level tie handling, and refresh obligations
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a hierarchy is a routing function, not a prestige ladder; its purpose is to send each question to the evidence capable of answering it
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to operationalize leading, adverse, and learning signals with denominators, cohort boundaries, feedback owners, and prohibition on unsupported benchmark claims

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checks role, decision options, hierarchy, artifact, examples, metrics, and adjacent routing, but it does not require verified run facts, model limits, query reproducibility, or source confirmation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because omitting any prerequisite can make a structurally polished packet irreproducible, misdirected, or semantically overconfident even when every original checklist item appears

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines one theme, all mapped sources, and one downstream review as capacity, but it does not model isolated-run setup, indexing freshness, query fan-out, response size, context selection, or semantic follow-up
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the service can answer many topology queries, but agent attention and graph freshness degrade when unrelated hypotheses, repositories, or change states share one investigation record
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: multiple repositories share assumed configuration, long-running changes outpace indexing, broad blast and smart-context calls become default, or several independent decisions are merged into a single final claim
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use workload controls to protect investigation coherence; administer process-level server capacity with measured operational data outside this reference
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the source-count capacity model with run lifecycle, freshness, query-depth, context, ownership, and split boundaries plus observable pressure signals
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the scarce resource is not graph storage alone but synchronized evidence: every additional question increases the chance that run state, context, and conclusion drift apart

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed sensibly limits stale-evidence retries and stops work on red gates, but it does not define retry identity, evidence change, safe query replay, or how reindexing affects entity keys and conclusions
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a retry that does not change state is repetition, while uncontrolled continuation on stale or ambiguous evidence compounds invalid conclusions across later queries
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: semantic disagreement triggers the same query, reindex loops indefinitely, concurrent agents refresh one run, entity keys survive unchecked across rebuilds, or a retry budget is reset by rewording the error
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply these controls to agent-operated local Parseltongue 1.7.2 runs and documentation workflows, not as a generic distributed-system retry policy
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add retry fingerprints, evidence-change prerequisites, entity revalidation, concurrency ownership, semantic success criteria, and modality-switch escalation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure protects epistemic state as much as compute: pausing prevents later reasoning from normalizing an unresolved substrate failure
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to retry only transient transport or freshness failures after changing an observable prerequisite, cap repeated attempts per failure class, replay from verified run identity, and stop graph work when substrate or model-fit gates remain red

### Question 10: What deeper deductions, second-order consequences, or additional insights follow, and how should they change the guidance?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that backpressure protects epistemic state as much as compute: pausing prevents later reasoning from normalizing an unresolved substrate failure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from a retry that does not change state is repetition, while uncontrolled continuation on stale or ambiguous evidence compounds invalid conclusions across later queries
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where semantic disagreement triggers the same query, reindex loops indefinitely, concurrent agents refresh one run, entity keys survive unchecked across rebuilds, or a retry budget is reset by rewording the error
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within apply these controls to agent-operated local Parseltongue 1.7.2 runs and documentation workflows, not as a generic distributed-system retry policy

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: switch to direct code reading, inspect server logs, use live API help, create a fresh isolated run, reduce traversal scope, defer to runtime tests, or escalate with the preserved evidence packet This changes how the section resolves when a failed Parseltongue operation deserves a retry, when investigation work must pause, and when the workflow should switch evidence modalities.

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed proposes source preservation and p95 under ten minutes for identifying a next action, but it does not define the timing boundary, task cohort, setup state, reviewer population, or baseline
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a fast wrong route is not useful performance, while including installation in every sample can obscure the repeat-use value of a prepared graph workflow
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one successful run is labeled p95, unmatched manual and graph cohorts are compared, setup costs disappear, reviewer time ends before source confirmation, or slow failures are excluded
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: evaluate documentation and investigation workflow efficiency, not Parseltongue server throughput or production service latency without a separate load-testing design
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the candidate target as unproven, split timing stages, add matched cohorts and correctness gates, expose percentile requirements, and offer low-sample alternatives
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the best performance unit is a verified decision transition, not a tool response, because endpoint latency may be negligible while interpretation dominates total effort

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, ownership boundaries, unbounded discovery, production traffic, and large codebases, but it does not specify run partitioning, cross-repository edges, change velocity, or dynamic integration limits
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because scaling a query over an incomplete model increases apparent coverage without adding missing deployment, message, reflection, generated, or organizational edges
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: separate services are merged by name, one graph is assumed to cover deployed topology, frequent changes outrun indexing, distributed agents write the same packet, or context compression drops uncertainty
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply this statement to analysis scope and evidence coordination, not to claims about maximum supported repository size or server throughput
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add workspace partitioning, revision and owner identity, cross-system evidence requirements, dynamic-edge routing, coordination rules, and measurable stop triggers
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale failure often begins as evidence-identity failure: once a response cannot be tied to one workspace snapshot and owner, more graph depth reduces trust
